color:black;"> </span> <small>5,000–7500</small></div> </td> <td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top;"> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff4200; color:black;"> </span> <small>7,500–10,000</small></div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff2c00; color:black;"> </span> <small>10,000–50,000</small></div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#cb0000; color:white;"> </span> <small>≥ 50,000</small></div> </td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div></div>
<p>The primary causes of death from HIV/AIDS are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opportunistic_infections" title="Opportunistic infections">opportunistic infections</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a>, both of which are frequently the result of the progressive failure of the immune system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InfectionBook2008_188-1"><a href="#cite_note-InfectionBook2008-188">[188]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cancer2005_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cancer2005-209">[209]</a></sup> Risk of cancer appears to increase once the CD4 count is below 500/μL.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deut2010_31-16"><a href="#cite_note-Deut2010-31">[31]</a></sup> The rate of clinical disease progression varies widely between individuals and has been shown to be affected by a number of factors such as a person's susceptibility and immune function;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tang_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tang-210">[210]</a></sup> their access to health care, the presence of co-infections;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morgan2_204-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morgan2-204">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lawn_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lawn-211">[211]</a></sup> and the particular strain (or strains) of the virus involved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell-212">[212]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Campbell2_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-Campbell2-213">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">Tuberculosis</a> co-infection is one of the leading causes of sickness and death in those with HIV/AIDS being present in a third of all HIV-infected people and causing 25% of HIV-related deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> HIV is also one of the most important risk factors for tuberculosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2011_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2011-215">[215]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis_C" title="Hepatitis C">Hepatitis C</a> is another very common co-infection where each disease increases the progression of the other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> The two most common cancers associated with HIV/AIDS are <a href="/wiki/Kaposi%27s_sarcoma" title="Kaposi's sarcoma">Kaposi's sarcoma</a> and AIDS-related <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hodgkin%27s_lymphoma" title="Non-Hodgkin's lymphoma">non-Hodgkin's lymphoma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cancer2005_209-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cancer2005-209">[209]</a></sup> Other cancers that are more frequent include <a href="/wiki/Anal_cancer" title="Anal cancer">anal cancer</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burkitt%27s_lymphoma" title="Burkitt's lymphoma">Burkitt's lymphoma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Primary_central_nervous_system_lymphoma" title="Primary central nervous system lymphoma">primary central nervous system lymphoma</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cervical_cancer" title="Cervical cancer">cervical cancer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deut2010_31-17"><a href="#cite_note-Deut2010-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup>
</p><p>Even with anti-retroviral treatment, over the long term HIV-infected people may experience <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS_dementia_complex" title="AIDS dementia complex">neurocognitive disorders</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Woods2009_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-Woods2009-218">[218]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Osteoporosis" title="Osteoporosis">osteoporosis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown2006_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brown2006-219">[219]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peripheral_neuropathy" title="Peripheral neuropathy">neuropathy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nicholas2007_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nicholas2007-220">[220]</a></sup> cancers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boshoff2002_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boshoff2002-221">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yarchoan2005_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yarchoan2005-222">[222]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nephropathy" title="Nephropathy">nephropathy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Post2009_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-Post2009-223">[223]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">cardiovascular disease</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burgoyne2008_175-1"><a href="#cite_note-Burgoyne2008-175">[175]</a></sup> Some conditions, such as <a href="/wiki/Lipodystrophy" title="Lipodystrophy">lipodystrophy</a>, may be caused both by HIV and its treatment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burgoyne2008_175-2"><a href="#cite_note-Burgoyne2008-175">[175]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Epidemiology">Epidemiology</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology_of_HIV/AIDS" title="Epidemiology of HIV/AIDS">Epidemiology of HIV/AIDS</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:522px"><div class="thumbimage noresize" style="width:520px;">
<div class="mw-graph mw-graph-always mw-graph-nofallback" data-graph-id="35009399471d3805d8492a3b83cec92ba0bb45b9" style="min-width:300px;min-height:265px"></div>
<small>See or edit <a class="extiw" href="https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Data:HIV_rates.tab" title="c:Data:HIV rates.tab">source data</a>. </small></div><div class="thumbcaption">Percentage of people with HIV/AIDS<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-224">[224]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Deaths-and-new-cases-of-hiv.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1978" data-file-width="3258" decoding="async" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Deaths-and-new-cases-of-hiv.png/400px-Deaths-and-new-cases-of-hiv.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Deaths-and-new-cases-of-hiv.png/600px-Deaths-and-new-cases-of-hiv.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Deaths-and-new-cases-of-hiv.png/800px-Deaths-and-new-cases-of-hiv.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Deaths-and-new-cases-of-hiv.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Trends in new cases and deaths per year from HIV/AIDS<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_224-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-224">[224]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Some authors consider HIV/AIDS a global <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">pandemic</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cohen2008_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cohen2008-225">[225]</a></sup> As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HIV/AIDS&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> approximately 36.7 million people worldwide have HIV, the number of new infections that year being about 1.8 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNAIDS2016_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNAIDS2016-226">[226]</a></sup> This is down from 3.1 million new infections in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN2013_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN2013-227">[227]</a></sup> Slightly over half the infected population are women and 2.1 million are children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNAIDS2016_226-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNAIDS2016-226">[226]</a></sup> It resulted in about 1 million deaths in 2016, down from a peak of 1.9 million in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNAIDS2016_226-2"><a href="#cite_note-UNAIDS2016-226">[226]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS_epidemiology#Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="AIDS epidemiology">Sub-Saharan Africa</a> is the region most affected. In 2010, an estimated 68% (22.9 million) of all HIV cases and 66% of all deaths (1.2 million) occurred in this region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN2011Thirty_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN2011Thirty-228">[228]</a></sup> This means that about 5% of the adult population is infected<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN2011Fifty_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN2011Fifty-229">[229]</a></sup> and it is believed to be the cause of 10% of all deaths in children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M117_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-M117-230">[230]</a></sup> Here, in contrast to other regions, women comprise nearly 60% of cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN2011Thirty_228-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN2011Thirty-228">[228]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> has the largest population of people with HIV of any country in the world at 5.9 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN2011Thirty_228-2"><a href="#cite_note-UN2011Thirty-228">[228]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> has fallen in the worst-affected countries due to HIV/AIDS; for example, in 2006 it was estimated that it had dropped from 65 to 35 years in <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kallings_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kallings-20">[20]</a></sup> Mother-to-child transmission in Botswana and South Africa, as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HIV/AIDS&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, has decreased to less than 5%, with improvement in many other African nations due to improved access to antiretroviral therapy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS_epidemiology#South_and_South-East_Asia" title="AIDS epidemiology">South &amp; South East Asia</a> is the second most affected; in 2010 this region contained an estimated 4 million cases or 12% of all people living with HIV resulting in approximately 250,000 deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN2011Fifty_229-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN2011Fifty-229">[229]</a></sup> Approximately 2.4 million of these cases are in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN2011Thirty_228-3"><a href="#cite_note-UN2011Thirty-228">[228]</a></sup>
</p><p>During 2008 in the United States approximately 1.2 million people were living with HIV, resulting in about 17,500 deaths. The US Centers for Disease Control and Prevention estimated that in that year, 20% of infected Americans were unaware of their infection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USAEPI2011_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-USAEPI2011-232">[232]</a></sup> As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HIV/AIDS&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> about 675,000 people have died of HIV/AIDS in the US since the beginning of the HIV epidemic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDC2016Today_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDC2016Today-233">[233]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="HIV/AIDS in the United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HIV/AIDS&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were approximately 101,200 cases which resulted in 594 deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> In Canada as of 2008, there were about 65,000 cases causing 53 deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> Between the first recognition of AIDS (in 1981) and 2009, it has led to nearly 30 million deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TotalDeath2010_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-TotalDeath2010-236">[236]</a></sup> Rates of HIV are lowest in North Africa and the Middle East (0.1% or less), <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a> (0.1%), and Western and Central Europe (0.2%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN2011Fifty_229-2"><a href="#cite_note-UN2011Fifty-229">[229]</a></sup> The worst-affected European countries, in 2009 and 2012 estimates, are <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, in decreasing order of prevalence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_HIV/AIDS" title="History of HIV/AIDS">History of HIV/AIDS</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a chronological guide, see <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_HIV/AIDS" title="Timeline of HIV/AIDS">Timeline of HIV/AIDS</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Category:HIV/AIDS_by_country" title="Category:HIV/AIDS by country">Category:HIV/AIDS by country</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery">Discovery</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mmwr-aids-July1981-report-101.png"><img alt="text of the Morbidity and Mortality Weekly Report newsletter" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3377" data-file-width="2360" decoding="async" height="315" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Mmwr-aids-July1981-report-101.png/220px-Mmwr-aids-July1981-report-101.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Mmwr-aids-July1981-report-101.png/330px-Mmwr-aids-July1981-report-101.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Mmwr-aids-July1981-report-101.png/440px-Mmwr-aids-July1981-report-101.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mmwr-aids-July1981-report-101.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <i><a href="/wiki/Morbidity_and_Mortality_Weekly_Report" title="Morbidity and Mortality Weekly Report">Morbidity and Mortality Weekly Report</a></i> reported in 1981 on what was later to be called "AIDS".</div></div></div>
<p>The first news story on the disease appeared on May 18, 1981, in the gay newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Native" title="New York Native">New York Native</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> AIDS was first clinically reported on June 5, 1981, with five cases in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M169_39-4"><a href="#cite_note-M169-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> The initial cases were a cluster of injecting drug users and gay men with no known cause of impaired immunity who showed symptoms of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pneumocystis_carinii" title="Pneumocystis carinii">Pneumocystis carinii</a></i> pneumonia (PCP), a rare opportunistic infection that was known to occur in people with very compromised immune systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMWR2_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-MMWR2-241">[241]</a></sup> Soon thereafter, a large number of homosexual men developed a generally rare skin cancer called <a href="/wiki/Kaposi%27s_sarcoma" title="Kaposi's sarcoma">Kaposi's sarcoma</a> (KS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid7287964_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid7287964-242">[242]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid6116083_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid6116083-243">[243]</a></sup> Many more cases of PCP and KS emerged, alerting U.S. Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC) and a CDC task force was formed to monitor the outbreak.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basavapathruni_2007_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-Basavapathruni_2007-244">[244]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the early days, the CDC did not have an official name for the disease, often referring to it by way of diseases associated with it, such as <a href="/wiki/Lymphadenopathy" title="Lymphadenopathy">lymphadenopathy</a>, the disease after which the discoverers of HIV originally named the virus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMWR1982a_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-MMWR1982a-245">[245]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Montagnier_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-Montagnier-246">[246]</a></sup> They also used <i>Kaposi's sarcoma and opportunistic infections</i>, the name by which a task force had been set up in 1981.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMWR1982b_247-0"><a href="#cite_note-MMWR1982b-247">[247]</a></sup> At one point the CDC referred to it as the "4H disease", as the syndrome seemed to affect heroin users, homosexuals, <a href="/wiki/Haemophilia" title="Haemophilia">hemophiliacs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haitians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SciRep470b_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-SciRep470b-249">[249]</a></sup> The term <i>GRID</i>, which stood for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay-related_immune_deficiency" title="Gay-related immune deficiency">gay-related immune deficiency</a>, had also been coined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Altman_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-Altman-250">[250]</a></sup> However, after determining that AIDS was not isolated to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay_community" title="Gay community">gay community</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMWR1982b_247-1"><a href="#cite_note-MMWR1982b-247">[247]</a></sup> it was realized that the term <i>GRID</i> was misleading, and the term <i>AIDS</i> was introduced at a meeting in July 1982.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kher_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kher-251">[251]</a></sup> By September 1982 the CDC started referring to the disease as AIDS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMWR1982c_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-MMWR1982c-252">[252]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1983, two separate research groups led by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Gallo" title="Robert Gallo">Robert Gallo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luc_Montagnier" title="Luc Montagnier">Luc Montagnier</a> declared that a novel retrovirus may have been infecting people with AIDS, and published their findings in the same issue of the journal <i><a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)">Science</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gallo_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gallo-253">[253]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Montagnier_246-1"><a href="#cite_note-Montagnier-246">[246]</a></sup> Gallo claimed a virus which his group had isolated from a person with AIDS was strikingly similar in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virus_structure" title="Virus structure">shape</a> to other <a href="/wiki/Human_T-lymphotropic_virus" title="Human T-lymphotropic virus">human T-lymphotropic viruses</a> (HTLVs) that his group had been the first to isolate. Gallo's group called their newly isolated virus HTLV-III. At the same time, Montagnier's group isolated a virus from a person presenting with swelling of the <a href="/wiki/Lymph_node" title="Lymph node">lymph nodes</a> of the neck and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asthenia" title="Asthenia">physical weakness</a>, two characteristic symptoms of AIDS. Contradicting the report from Gallo's group, Montagnier and his colleagues showed that core proteins of this virus were immunologically different from those of HTLV-I. Montagnier's group named their isolated virus lymphadenopathy-associated virus (LAV).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basavapathruni_2007_244-1"><a href="#cite_note-Basavapathruni_2007-244">[244]</a></sup> As these two viruses turned out to be the same, in 1986, LAV and HTLV-III were renamed HIV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SIV_primates.jpg"><img alt="three primates possible sources of HIV" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1487" data-file-width="3300" decoding="async" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/SIV_primates.jpg/300px-SIV_primates.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/SIV_primates.jpg/450px-SIV_primates.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/SIV_primates.jpg/600px-SIV_primates.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SIV_primates.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Left to right: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_green_monkey" title="African green monkey">African green monkey</a> source of <a href="/wiki/Simian_immunodeficiency_virus" title="Simian immunodeficiency virus">SIV</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sooty_mangabey" title="Sooty mangabey">sooty mangabey</a> source of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HIV-2" title="HIV-2">HIV-2</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_chimpanzee" title="Common chimpanzee">chimpanzee</a> source of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HIV-1" title="HIV-1">HIV-1</a></div></div></div>
<p>The origin of HIV / AIDS and the circumstances that led to its emergence remain unsolved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thomas_Gilbert_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas_Gilbert-255">[255]</a></sup>
</p><p>Both HIV-1 and HIV-2 are believed to have originated in non-human <a href="/wiki/Primate" title="Primate">primates</a> in West-central Africa and were <a href="/wiki/Zoonosis" title="Zoonosis">transferred to humans</a> in the early 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Orgin2011_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Orgin2011-21">[21]</a></sup> HIV-1 appears to have originated in southern <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> through the evolution of SIV(cpz), a <a href="/wiki/Simian_immunodeficiency_virus" title="Simian immunodeficiency virus">simian immunodeficiency virus</a> (SIV) that infects wild <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_chimpanzee" title="Common chimpanzee">chimpanzees</a> (HIV-1 descends from the SIVcpz endemic in the chimpanzee subspecies <i>Pan troglodytes troglodytes</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid9989410_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid9989410-256">[256]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Keele_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-Keele-257">[257]</a></sup> The closest relative of HIV-2 is SIV (smm), a virus of the <a href="/wiki/Sooty_mangabey" title="Sooty mangabey">sooty mangabey</a> (<i>Cercocebus atys atys</i>), an <a href="/wiki/Old_World_monkey" title="Old World monkey">Old World monkey</a> living in coastal West Africa (from southern <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> to western <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reeves_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reeves-100">[100]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/New_World_monkey" title="New World monkey">New World monkeys</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Night_monkey" title="Night monkey">owl monkey</a> are resistant to <a href="/wiki/Subtypes_of_HIV" title="Subtypes of HIV">HIV-1</a> infection, possibly because of a genomic <a href="/wiki/Fusion_gene" title="Fusion gene">fusion</a> of two viral resistance genes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goodier_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-Goodier-258">[258]</a></sup> HIV-1 is thought to have jumped the species barrier on at least three separate occasions, giving rise to the three groups of the virus, M, N, and O.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sharp2001_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sharp2001-259">[259]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is evidence that humans who participate in <a href="/wiki/Bushmeat" title="Bushmeat">bushmeat</a> activities, either as hunters or as bushmeat vendors, commonly acquire SIV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kalish2005_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kalish2005-260">[260]</a></sup> However, SIV is a weak virus which is typically suppressed by the human immune system within weeks of infection. It is thought that several transmissions of the virus from individual to individual in quick succession are necessary to allow it enough time to mutate into HIV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marx2001_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marx2001-261">[261]</a></sup> Furthermore, due to its relatively low person-to-person transmission rate, SIV can only spread throughout the population in the presence of one or more high-risk transmission channels, which are thought to have been absent in Africa before the 20th century.
</p><p>Specific proposed high-risk transmission channels, allowing the virus to adapt to humans and spread throughout society, depend on the proposed timing of the animal-to-human crossing. Genetic studies of the virus suggest that the most recent common ancestor of the HIV-1 M group dates back to <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1910.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Worobey2008_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-Worobey2008-262">[262]</a></sup> Proponents of this dating link the HIV epidemic with the emergence of <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a> and growth of large colonial African cities, leading to social changes, including a higher degree of sexual promiscuity, the spread of prostitution, and the accompanying high frequency of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genital_ulcer_disease" title="Genital ulcer disease">genital ulcer diseases</a> (such as <a href="/wiki/Syphilis" title="Syphilis">syphilis</a>) in nascent colonial cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sousa2010_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sousa2010-263">[263]</a></sup> While transmission rates of HIV during vaginal intercourse are low under regular circumstances, they are increased manyfold if one of the partners has a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexually_transmitted_disease" title="Sexually transmitted disease">sexually transmitted infection</a> causing genital ulcers. Early 1900s colonial cities were notable for their high prevalence of prostitution and genital ulcers, to the degree that, as of 1928, as many as 45% of female residents of eastern <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a> were thought to have been prostitutes, and, as of 1933, around 15% of all residents of the same city had syphilis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sousa2010_263-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sousa2010-263">[263]</a></sup>
</p><p>An alternative view holds that unsafe medical practices in Africa after World War II, such as unsterile reuse of single-use syringes during mass vaccination, antibiotic and anti-malaria treatment campaigns, were the initial vector that allowed the virus to adapt to humans and spread.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marx2001_261-1"><a href="#cite_note-Marx2001-261">[261]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chitnis2000_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chitnis2000-264">[264]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNeil_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-McNeil-265">[265]</a></sup>
</p><p>The earliest well-documented case of HIV in a human dates back to 1959 in the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Congo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zhu_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zhu-266">[266]</a></sup>  The virus may have been present in the U.S. as early as the mid-to-late 1950s, as a sixteen-year-old male named <a href="/wiki/Robert_Rayford" title="Robert Rayford">Robert Rayford</a> presented with symptoms in 1966 and died in 1969. In the 1970s, there were cases of getting parasites and becoming sick with what was called “gay bowel disease,” but what is now suspected to have been AIDS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup>
</p><p>The earliest retrospectively described case of AIDS is believed to have been in Norway beginning in 1966.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> In July 1960, in the wake of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo#Independence_and_political_crisis_(1960–1965)" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congo's independence</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> recruited <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">Francophone</a> experts and technicians from all over the world to assist in filling administrative gaps left by <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, who did not leave behind an African elite to run the country. By 1962, Haitians made up the second-largest group of well-educated experts (out of the 48 national groups recruited), that totaled around 4500 in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pépin_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pépin-270">[270]</a></sup> Dr. Jacques Pépin, a Canadian author of <i>The Origins of AIDS</i>, stipulates that Haiti was one of HIV's entry points to the U.S. and that a Haitian may have carried HIV back across the Atlantic in the 1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pépin_270-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pépin-270">[270]</a></sup> Although there was known to have been at least one case of AIDS in the U.S. from 1966,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup> the vast majority of infections occurring outside sub-Saharan Africa (including the U.S.) can be traced back to a single unknown individual who became infected with HIV in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> and then brought the infection to the U.S. at some time around 1969.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thomas_Gilbert_255-1"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas_Gilbert-255">[255]</a></sup> The epidemic then rapidly spread among high-risk groups (initially, sexually promiscuous men who have sex with men). By 1978, the prevalence of HIV-1 among gay male residents of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> was estimated at 5%, suggesting that several thousand individuals in the country had been infected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thomas_Gilbert_255-2"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas_Gilbert-255">[255]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_culture">Society and culture</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stigma">Stigma</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Discrimination_against_people_with_HIV/AIDS" title="Discrimination against people with HIV/AIDS">Discrimination against people with HIV/AIDS</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:164px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ryan_White.jpg"><img alt="A teenage male with the hand of another resting on his left shoulder smiling for the camera" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="216" data-file-width="162" decoding="async" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/97/Ryan_White.jpg" width="162"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ryan_White.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ryan_White" title="Ryan White">Ryan White</a> became a <a href="/wiki/Poster_child" title="Poster child">poster child</a> for HIV after being expelled from school because he was infected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>AIDS stigma exists around the world in a variety of ways, including <a href="/wiki/Shunning" title="Shunning">ostracism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_rejection" title="Social rejection">rejection</a>, discrimination and avoidance of HIV-infected people; compulsory HIV testing without prior <a href="/wiki/Consent" title="Consent">consent</a> or protection of <a href="/wiki/Confidentiality" title="Confidentiality">confidentiality</a>; violence against HIV-infected individuals or people who are perceived to be infected with HIV; and the <a href="/wiki/Quarantine" title="Quarantine">quarantine</a> of HIV-infected individuals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNAIDS2006Ch4_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-UNAIDS2006Ch4-23">[23]</a></sup> Stigma-related violence or the fear of violence prevents many people from seeking HIV testing, returning for their results, or securing treatment, possibly turning what could be a manageable chronic illness into a death sentence and perpetuating the spread of HIV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ogden_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ogden-273">[273]</a></sup>
</p><p>AIDS stigma has been further divided into the following three categories:
</p>
<ul><li><i>Instrumental AIDS stigma</i>—a reflection of the fear and apprehension that are likely to be associated with any deadly and transmissible illness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herek1999_274-0"><a href="#cite_note-Herek1999-274">[274]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Symbolic AIDS stigma</i>—the use of HIV/AIDS to express attitudes toward the social groups or lifestyles perceived to be associated with the disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herek1999_274-1"><a href="#cite_note-Herek1999-274">[274]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Courtesy AIDS stigma</i>—stigmatization of people connected to the issue of HIV/AIDS or HIV-positive people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Snyder_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-Snyder-275">[275]</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Often, AIDS stigma is expressed in conjunction with one or more other stigmas, particularly those associated with homosexuality, <a href="/wiki/Bisexuality" title="Bisexuality">bisexuality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Promiscuity" title="Promiscuity">promiscuity</a>, prostitution, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intravenous_drug_use_(recreational)" title="Intravenous drug use (recreational)">intravenous drug use</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup>
</p><p>In many <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed countries</a>, there is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS_and_homosexuality" title="AIDS and homosexuality">an association between AIDS and homosexuality or bisexuality</a>, and this association is correlated with higher levels of sexual prejudice, such as <a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">anti-homosexual</a> or <a href="/wiki/Biphobia" title="Biphobia">anti-bisexual</a> attitudes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herek2002_277-0"><a href="#cite_note-Herek2002-277">[277]</a></sup> There is also a perceived association between AIDS and all male-male sexual behavior, including sex between uninfected men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herek1999_274-2"><a href="#cite_note-Herek1999-274">[274]</a></sup> However, the dominant mode of spread worldwide for HIV remains heterosexual transmission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup> To get a better understanding of the anti-homosexual attitudes around AIDs the musical <i>Rent</i> explores this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2003, as part of an overall reform of marriage and population legislation, it became legal for those diagnosed with AIDS to marry in China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Medicine" title="National Library of Medicine">U.S. National Library of Medicine</a> developed a traveling exhibition titled <i>Surviving and Thriving: AIDS, Politics, and Culture</i>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup> this covered medical research, the U.S. government's response, and personal stories from people with AIDS, caregivers, and activists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_impact">Economic impact</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economic_impact_of_HIV/AIDS" title="Economic impact of HIV/AIDS">Economic impact of HIV/AIDS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cost_of_HIV_treatment" title="Cost of HIV treatment">Cost of HIV treatment</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg"><img alt="A graph showing several increasing lines followed by a sharp fall of the lines starting in the mid-1980s to 1990s" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="335" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg/330px-Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg/495px-Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg/660px-Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Changes in life expectancy in some African countries, 1960–2012</div></div></div>
<p>HIV/AIDS affects the economics of both individuals and countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M117_230-1"><a href="#cite_note-M117-230">[230]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> of the most affected countries has decreased due to the lack of <a href="/wiki/Human_capital" title="Human capital">human capital</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M117_230-2"><a href="#cite_note-M117-230">[230]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bell-et-al-2003_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bell-et-al-2003-283">[283]</a></sup> Without proper nutrition, health care and medicine, large numbers of people die from AIDS-related complications. Before death they will not only be unable to work, but will also require significant medical care. It is estimated that as of 2007 there were 12 million <a href="/wiki/AIDS_orphan" title="AIDS orphan">AIDS orphans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M117_230-3"><a href="#cite_note-M117-230">[230]</a></sup> Many are cared for by elderly grandparents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greener_284-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greener-284">[284]</a></sup>
</p><p>Returning to work after beginning treatment for HIV/AIDS is difficult, and affected people often work less than the average worker. <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">Unemployment</a> in people with HIV/AIDS also is associated with <a href="/wiki/Suicidal_ideation" title="Suicidal ideation">suicidal ideation</a>, memory problems, and social isolation. Employment increases <a href="/wiki/Self-esteem" title="Self-esteem">self-esteem</a>, sense of dignity, confidence, and <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a> for people with HIV/AIDS. Anti-retroviral treatment may help people with HIV/AIDS work more, and may increase the chance that a person with HIV/AIDS will be employed (low-quality evidence).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup>
</p><p>By affecting mainly young adults, AIDS reduces the taxable population, in turn reducing the resources available for <a href="/wiki/Government_spending" title="Government spending">public expenditures</a> such as education and health services not related to AIDS, resulting in increasing pressure on the state's finances and slower growth of the economy. This causes a slower growth of the tax base, an effect that is reinforced if there are growing expenditures on treating the sick, training (to replace sick workers), sick pay, and caring for AIDS orphans. This is especially true if the sharp increase in adult mortality shifts the responsibility from the family to the government in caring for these orphans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greener_284-1"><a href="#cite_note-Greener-284">[284]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the household level, AIDS causes both loss of income and increased spending on healthcare. A study in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" title="Côte d'Ivoire">Côte d'Ivoire</a> showed that households having a person with HIV/AIDS spent twice as much on medical expenses as other households. This additional expenditure also leaves less income to spend on education and other personal or family investment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WBank_286-0"><a href="#cite_note-WBank-286">[286]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion_and_AIDS">Religion and AIDS</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_and_HIV/AIDS" title="Religion and HIV/AIDS">Religion and HIV/AIDS</a></div>
<p>The topic of religion and AIDS has become highly controversial, primarily because some religious authorities have publicly declared their opposition to the use of condoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thirty_years_after_AIDS_discovery,_appreciation_growing_for_Catholic_approach_288-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thirty_years_after_AIDS_discovery,_appreciation_growing_for_Catholic_approach-288">[288]</a></sup> The religious approach to prevent the spread of AIDS, according to a report by American health expert Matthew Hanley titled <i>The Catholic Church and the Global AIDS Crisis</i>, argues that cultural changes are needed, including a re-emphasis on fidelity within marriage and sexual abstinence outside of it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thirty_years_after_AIDS_discovery,_appreciation_growing_for_Catholic_approach_288-1"><a href="#cite_note-Thirty_years_after_AIDS_discovery,_appreciation_growing_for_Catholic_approach-288">[288]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some religious organizations have claimed that prayer can cure HIV/AIDS. In 2011, the BBC reported that some churches in London were claiming that prayer would cure AIDS, and the <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Hackney" title="London Borough of Hackney">Hackney</a>-based Centre for the Study of Sexual Health and HIV reported that several people stopped taking their medication, sometimes on the direct advice of their pastor, leading to many deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC18102011_289-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC18102011-289">[289]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synagogue_Church_Of_All_Nations" title="Synagogue Church Of All Nations">Synagogue Church Of All Nations</a> advertised an "anointing water" to promote God's healing, although the group denies advising people to stop taking medication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC18102011_289-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC18102011-289">[289]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_portrayal">Media portrayal</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_portrayal_of_HIV/AIDS" title="Media portrayal of HIV/AIDS">Media portrayal of HIV/AIDS</a></div>
<p>One of the first high-profile cases of AIDS was the American <a href="/wiki/Rock_Hudson" title="Rock Hudson">Rock Hudson</a>, a gay actor who had been married and divorced earlier in life, who died on October 2, 1985, having announced that he had had the virus on July 25 that year. He had been diagnosed during 1984.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup> A notable British casualty of AIDS that year was <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Eden,_2nd_Earl_of_Avon" title="Nicholas Eden, 2nd Earl of Avon">Nicholas Eden</a>, a gay politician and son of the late prime minister <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Eden" title="Anthony Eden">Anthony Eden</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup> On November 24, 1991, the virus claimed the life of British rock star <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury" title="Freddie Mercury">Freddie Mercury</a>, lead singer of the band <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>, who died from an AIDS-related illness having only revealed the diagnosis on the previous day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup> However, he had been diagnosed as HIV-positive in 1987. Mercury had also begun to show signs of the virus as early as 1982.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup> One of the first high-profile heterosexual cases of the virus was American tennis player <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Ashe" title="Arthur Ashe">Arthur Ashe</a>. He was diagnosed as HIV-positive on August 31, 1988, having contracted the virus from blood transfusions during heart surgery earlier in the 1980s. Further tests within 24 hours of the initial diagnosis revealed that Ashe had AIDS, but he did not tell the public about his diagnosis until April 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> He died as a result on February 6, 1993, aged 49.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup>
</p><p>Therese Frare's photograph of gay activist <a href="/wiki/David_Kirby_(activist)" title="David Kirby (activist)">David Kirby</a>, as he lay dying from AIDS while surrounded by family, was taken in April 1990. <i><a href="/wiki/Life_(magazine)" title="Life (magazine)">Life</a></i> magazine said the photo became the one image "most powerfully identified with the HIV/AIDS epidemic." The photo was displayed in <i>Life</i>, was the winner of the <a href="/wiki/World_Press_Photo" title="World Press Photo">World Press Photo</a>, and acquired worldwide notoriety after being used in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Colors_of_Benetton" title="United Colors of Benetton">United Colors of Benetton</a> advertising campaign in 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many famous artists and AIDS activists such as <a href="/wiki/Larry_Kramer" title="Larry Kramer">Larry Kramer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diamanda_Gal%C3%A1s" title="Diamanda Galás">Diamanda Galás</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rosa_von_Praunheim" title="Rosa von Praunheim">Rosa von Praunheim</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeutscheWelle_297-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeutscheWelle-297">[297]</a></sup> campaign for AIDS education and the rights of those affected. These artists worked with various media formats.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criminal_transmission">Criminal transmission</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criminal_transmission_of_HIV" title="Criminal transmission of HIV">Criminal transmission of HIV</a></div>
<p>Criminal transmission of HIV is the <a href="/wiki/Intention_(criminal_law)" title="Intention (criminal law)">intentional</a> or <a href="/wiki/Recklessness_(law)" title="Recklessness (law)">reckless</a> infection of a person with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_immunodeficiency_virus" title="Human immunodeficiency virus">human immunodeficiency virus</a> (HIV). Some countries or jurisdictions, including some areas of the United States, have laws that criminalize HIV transmission or exposure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> Others may charge the accused under laws enacted before the HIV pandemic.
</p><p>In 1996, Ugandan-born Canadian <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Aziga" title="Johnson Aziga">Johnson Aziga</a> was diagnosed with HIV; he subsequently had unprotected sex with eleven women without disclosing his diagnosis. By 2003, seven had contracted HIV; two died from complications related to AIDS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup> Aziga was convicted of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First-degree_murder" title="First-degree murder">first-degree murder</a> and sentenced to <a href="/wiki/Life_imprisonment_in_Canada" title="Life imprisonment in Canada">life imprisonment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Misconceptions">Misconceptions</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Misconceptions_about_HIV/AIDS" title="Misconceptions about HIV/AIDS">Misconceptions about HIV/AIDS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Discredited_HIV/AIDS_origins_theories" title="Discredited HIV/AIDS origins theories">Discredited HIV/AIDS origins theories</a></div>
<p>There are many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Misconceptions_about_HIV_and_AIDS" title="Misconceptions about HIV and AIDS">misconceptions about HIV and AIDS</a>. Three misconceptions are that AIDS can spread through casual contact, that <a href="/wiki/Virgin_cleansing_myth" title="Virgin cleansing myth">sexual intercourse with a virgin</a> will cure AIDS,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> and that HIV can infect only gay men and drug users.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WIFANG_305-0"><a href="#cite_note-WIFANG-305">[305]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RASEFSS_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-RASEFSS-306">[306]</a></sup> In 2014, some among the British public wrongly thought one could get HIV from kissing (16%), sharing a glass (5%), spitting (16%), a public toilet seat (4%), and coughing or sneezing (5%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup> Other misconceptions are that any act of anal intercourse between two uninfected gay men can lead to HIV infection, and that open discussion of HIV and homosexuality in schools will lead to increased rates of AIDS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup>
</p><p>A small group of individuals continue to dispute the connection between HIV and AIDS,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Duesberg_310-0"><a href="#cite_note-Duesberg-310">[310]</a></sup> the existence of HIV itself, or the validity of HIV testing and treatment methods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kalichman_311-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kalichman-311">[311]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SmithNovella_312-0"><a href="#cite_note-SmithNovella-312">[312]</a></sup> These claims, known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS_denialism" title="AIDS denialism">AIDS denialism</a>, have been examined and rejected by the scientific community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-consensus_313-0"><a href="#cite_note-consensus-313">[313]</a></sup> However, they have had a significant political impact, particularly <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_denialism_in_South_Africa" title="HIV/AIDS denialism in South Africa">in South Africa</a>, where the government's official embrace of AIDS denialism (1999–2005) was responsible for its ineffective response to that country's AIDS epidemic, and has been blamed for hundreds of thousands of avoidable deaths and HIV infections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup>
</p><p>Several discredited <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theories" title="Conspiracy theories">conspiracy theories</a> have held that HIV was created by scientists, either inadvertently or deliberately. <a href="/wiki/Operation_INFEKTION" title="Operation INFEKTION">Operation INFEKTION</a> was a worldwide Soviet <a href="/wiki/Active_measures" title="Active measures">active measures</a> operation to spread the claim that the United States had created HIV/AIDS. Surveys show that a significant number of people believed—and continue to believe—in such claims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-infektion_317-0"><a href="#cite_note-infektion-317">[317]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the peak of the HIV/AIDS outbreak, there was also misinformation spread from some governmental institutions. For example, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Fauci" title="Anthony Fauci">Anthony Fauci</a>, head of the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Allergy_and_Infectious_Diseases" title="National Institute of Allergy and Infectious Diseases">National Institute of Allergy and Infectious Diseases</a> during the AIDS outbreak, stated in the context of a conversation about childhood infections, “if the close contact of a child is a household contact, perhaps there will be a certain number of cases of individuals who are just living with and in close contact with someone with AIDS, or at risk of AIDS, who does not necessarily have to have intimate sexual contact or share a needle, but just the ordinary close contact that one sees in normal interpersonal relations.”<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup> This and similar statements made by governmental agencies potentially fueled the unfounded fear that the public had that AIDS could be spread by ordinary close contact rather than through sexual or fluid transmission as is most commonly the case.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_research" title="HIV/AIDS research">HIV/AIDS research</a></div>
<p>HIV/AIDS research includes all <a href="/wiki/Medical_research" title="Medical research">medical research</a> which attempts to prevent, treat, or cure HIV/AIDS, along with fundamental research about the nature of HIV as an infectious agent, and about AIDS as the disease caused by HIV.
</p><p>Many governments and research institutions participate in HIV/AIDS research. This research includes behavioral <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_interventions" title="Health interventions">health interventions</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Sex_education" title="Sex education">sex education</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Drug_development" title="Drug development">drug development</a>, such as research into <a href="/wiki/Microbicides_for_sexually_transmitted_diseases" title="Microbicides for sexually transmitted diseases">microbicides for sexually transmitted diseases</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HIV_vaccines" title="HIV vaccines">HIV vaccines</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antiretroviral_drugs" title="Antiretroviral drugs">antiretroviral drugs</a>. Other medical research areas include the topics of <a href="/wiki/Pre-exposure_prophylaxis" title="Pre-exposure prophylaxis">pre-exposure prophylaxis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Post-exposure_prophylaxis" title="Post-exposure prophylaxis">post-exposure prophylaxis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Circumcision_and_HIV" title="Circumcision and HIV">circumcision and HIV</a>. Public health officials, researchers, and programs can gain a more comprehensive picture of the barriers they face, and the efficacy of current approaches to HIV treatment and prevention, by tracking standard HIV indicators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup> Use of common indicators is an increasing focus of development organizations and researchers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup>
</p>
